style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;v&#39; in &#39;vie&#39;">v</span><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span><span title="&#39;f&#39; in &#39;find&#39;">f</span><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> is a British <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a> conglomerate, with headquarters in London.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> It predominantly operates services in the regions of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>. Among <a href="/wiki/List_of_mobile_network_operators" title="List of mobile network operators">mobile operator groups</a> globally, Vodafone ranked 4th (behind <a href="/wiki/China_Mobile" title="China Mobile">China Mobile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bharti_Airtel" title="Bharti Airtel">Bharti Airtel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Idea" class="mw-redirect" title="Vodafone Idea">Vodafone Idea</a>) in the number of mobile customers (313 million) as of  2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Vodafone owns and operates networks in 25 countries, and has partner networks in 47 further countries.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Global_Enterprise" title="Vodafone Global Enterprise">Vodafone Global Enterprise</a> division provides <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a> and IT services to corporate clients in 150 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Vodafone has a primary listing on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> and is a constituent of the <a href="/wiki/FTSE_100_Index" title="FTSE 100 Index">FTSE 100 Index</a>. It had a <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalisation</a> of approximately \xc2\xa352.5&#160;billion as of  10&#160;February&#160;2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the eighth-largest of any company listed on the London Stock Exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The company has a secondary listing on <a href="/wiki/NASDAQ" title="NASDAQ">NASDAQ</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Evolution_as_a_Racal_Telecom_brand:_1980_to_1991"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Evolution as a Racal Telecom brand: 1980 to 1991</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Vodafone_Group,_then_Vodafone_Airtouch_plc:_1991_to_2000"><span class="tocnumber">2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Vodafone Group, then Vodafone Airtouch plc: 1991 to 2000</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Vodafone_Group_plc:_2000_to_present"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Vodafone Group plc: 2000 to present</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="toclevel-3 tocsection-19"><a href="#New_Zealand"><span class="tocnumber">4.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">New Zealand</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a Enterprise</span></span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Products_and_services"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Products and services</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Mobile_money_transfer_services"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Mobile money transfer services</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#mHealth_services"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">mHealth services</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Vodafone_Foundation"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Vodafone Foundation</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Corporate_affairs"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Corporate affairs</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Senior_management"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Senior management</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Financial_results"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Financial results</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#Criticisms"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Criticisms</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Tax_avoidance"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Tax avoidance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Communications_blackout_during_the_Arab_Spring"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Communications blackout during the Arab Spring</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#Poor_customer_service"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Poor customer service</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Unlimited_roaming_costs_on_stolen_phones"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Unlimited roaming costs on stolen phones</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-39"><a href="#Breaches_of_consumer_protection_rules"><span class="tocnumber">7.5</span> <span class="toctext">Breaches of consumer protection rules</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#Surveillance_infrastructure"><span class="tocnumber">7.6</span> <span class="toctext">Surveillance infrastructure</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The name Vodafone comes from <b>vo</b>ice <b>da</b>ta <b>fone</b> (the latter a <a href="/wiki/Sensational_spelling" title="Sensational spelling">sensational spelling</a> of "<a href="/wiki/Telephone" title="Telephone">phone</a>"), chosen by the company to "reflect the provision of voice and data services over mobile phones".<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The evolution of Vodafone started in 1982 with the establishment of the Racal Strategic Radio Ltd subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Racal" title="Racal">Racal Electronics</a>, the UK\'s largest maker of military radio technology, which formed a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Millicom" title="Millicom">Millicom</a> called \'Racal\', which evolved into the present day Vodafone.<sup id="cite_ref-VOD-G-H-01_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOD-G-H-01-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VOD-G-H-02_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOD-G-H-02-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VOD-G-H-03_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOD-G-H-03-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evolution_as_a_Racal_Telecom_brand:_1980_to_1991">Evolution as a Racal Telecom brand: 1980 to 1991</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Evolution as a Racal Telecom brand: 1980 to 1991">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vodafone_1984_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a0/Vodafone_1984_logo.svg/220px-Vodafone_1984_logo.svg.png" width="220" height="35" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a0/Vodafone_1984_logo.svg/330px-Vodafone_1984_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a0/Vodafone_1984_logo.svg/440px-Vodafone_1984_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="263" data-file-height="42" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vodafone_1984_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vodafone\'s original logo, used from 1991 to 1997</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1980, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Harrison" title="Ernest Harrison">Ernest Harrison</a>, the then chairman of Racal Electronics, agreed to a deal with <a href="/wiki/Lord_Weinstock" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Weinstock">Lord Weinstock</a> of the <a href="/wiki/General_Electric_Company_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="General Electric Company plc">General Electric Company</a> to allow Racal to access some of GEC\'s tactical battlefield radio technology. The head of Racal\'s military radio division, <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Whent" title="Gerry Whent">Gerry Whent</a>, was briefed by Ernest Harrison to drive the company into commercial mobile radio. Whent visited a mobile radio factory run by <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a> (unrelated to GEC) in <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, USA the same year to understand the commercial use of military radio technology.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jan_Stenbeck" title="Jan Stenbeck">Jan Stenbeck</a>, head of a growing Swedish conglomerate, set up an American company, Millicom, Inc. and approached Racal\'s Whent in July 1982 about bidding jointly for the UK\'s second cellular radio licence. The two struck a deal giving Racal 60% of the new company, Racal-Millicom, Ltd, and Millicom 40%. Due to UK concerns about foreign ownership, the terms were revised, and in December 1982, the Racal-Milicom partnership was awarded the second UK mobile phone network license.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Final ownership of Racal-Millicom, Ltd was 80% Racal, with Millicom holding 15% plus royalties and venture firm Hambros Technology Trust holding 5%. According to the UK Secretary of State for Industry, "the bid submitted by Racal-Millicom Ltd\xe2\x80\xa6 provided the best prospect for early national coverage by cellular radio."<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Vodafone was launched on 1 January 1985 under the new name, Racal-Vodafone (Holdings) Ltd,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> with its first office based in the Courtyard in <a href="/wiki/Newbury,_Berkshire" title="Newbury, Berkshire">Newbury</a>, Berkshire, and<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> shortly thereafter Racal Strategic Radio was renamed Racal Telecommunications Group Limited.<sup id="cite_ref-sec_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sec-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> On 29 December 1986, Racal Electronics issued shares to the minority shareholders of Vodafone worth GB\xc2\xa3110&#160;million, and Vodafone became a fully owned brand of Racal.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 26 October 1988, Racal Telecom, majority held by Racal Electronics, went public on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> with 20% of its stock floated. The successful flotation led to a situation where Racal\'s stake in Racal Telecom was valued more than the whole of Racal Electronics. Under stock market pressure to realise full value for shareholders, Racal demerged Racal Telecom in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VOD-G-H-04_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOD-G-H-04-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Vodafone_Group.2C_then_Vodafone_Airtouch_plc:_1991_to_2000"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Vodafone_Group,_then_Vodafone_Airtouch_plc:_1991_to_2000">Vodafone Group, then Vodafone Airtouch plc: 1991 to 2000</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Vodafone Group, then Vodafone Airtouch plc: 1991 to 2000">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 16 September 1991, Racal Telecom was demerged from Racal Electronics as <b>Vodafone Group</b>, with Gerry Whent as its CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 1996, Vodafone acquired the two-thirds of Talkland it did not already own for \xc2\xa330.6&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> On 19 November 1996, in a defensive move, Vodafone purchased <a href="/wiki/Peoples_Phone" class="mw-redirect" title="Peoples Phone">Peoples Phone</a> for \xc2\xa377&#160;million, a 181 store chain whose customers were overwhelmingly using Vodafone\'s network.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In a similar move the company acquired the 80% of Astec Communications that it did not own, a service provider with 21 stores.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 1997, Gerald Whent retired and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Gent" title="Chris Gent">Christopher Gent</a> took over as the CEO. The same year, Vodafone introduced its <i>Speechmark</i> logo, composed of a <a href="/wiki/Quotation_mark" title="Quotation mark">quotation mark</a> in a circle, with the O\'s in the Vodafone logotype representing opening and closing quotation marks and suggesting conversation.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 29 June 1999, Vodafone completed its purchase of <a href="/wiki/AirTouch_Communications" class="mw-redirect" title="AirTouch Communications">AirTouch Communications, Inc.</a> and changed its name to <b>Vodafone Airtouch plc</b>. The merged company commenced trading on 30 June 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The acquisition gave Vodafone a 35% share of <a href="/wiki/Mannesmann" title="Mannesmann">Mannesmann</a>, owner of the largest German mobile network.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> To gain anti-trust approval for the merger, Vodafone sold its 17.2% stake in Mannesmann\'s German competitor, <a href="/wiki/E-Plus" title="E-Plus">E-Plus Mobilfunk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 21 September 1999, Vodafone agreed to merge its US wireless assets with those of <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Communications" title="Verizon Communications">Bell Atlantic Corp</a> to form <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Wireless" title="Verizon Wireless">Verizon Wireless</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The merger was completed on 4 April 2000, just a few months prior to Bell Atlantic\'s merger with <a href="/wiki/GTE" title="GTE">GTE</a> to form Verizon Communications, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 1999, Vodafone made an unsolicited bid for <a href="/wiki/Mannesmann" title="Mannesmann">Mannesmann</a>, which was rejected. Vodafone\'s interest in Mannesmann had been increased by the latter purchase of <a href="/wiki/Orange_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Orange (UK)">Orange</a>, the UK mobile operator.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Chris Gent would later say Mannesmann\'s move into the UK broke a "gentleman\'s agreement" not to compete in each other\'s home territory.<sup id="cite_ref-mann_merger_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mann_merger-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The hostile takeover provoked strong protest in Germany, and a "titanic struggle" which saw Mannesmann resist Vodafone\'s efforts. However, on 3 February 2000, the Mannesmann board agreed to an increased offer of \xc2\xa3112&#160;billion, then the largest corporate merger ever.<sup id="cite_ref-mann_merger_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mann_merger-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> approved the merger in April 2000 when Vodafone agreed to divest the \'Orange\' brand, which was acquired in May 2000 by <a href="/wiki/Orange_S.A." title="Orange S.A.">France T\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa9com</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vodafone_Group_plc:_2000_to_present">Vodafone Group plc: 2000 to present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Vodafone Group plc: 2000 to present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Bucuresti_street_scene_-i.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/A_Bucuresti_street_scene_-i.jpg/170px-A_Bucuresti_street_scene_-i.jpg" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/A_Bucuresti_street_scene_-i.jpg/255px-A_Bucuresti_street_scene_-i.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/A_Bucuresti_street_scene_-i.jpg/340px-A_Bucuresti_street_scene_-i.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3872" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Bucuresti_street_scene_-i.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Romania" title="Vodafone Romania">Vodafone Romania</a> in Bucharest</div></div></div>\n<p>On 28 July 2000, the Company reverted to its former name, <b>Vodafone Group plc</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 17 December 2001, Vodafone introduced the concept of "Partner Networks", by signing <a href="/wiki/TDC_A/S" title="TDC A/S">TDC</a> Mobil of Denmark. The new concept involved the introduction of Vodafone international services to the local market, without the need of investment by Vodafone. The concept would be used to extend the Vodafone brand and services into markets where it does not have stakes in local operators. Vodafone services would be marketed under the dual-brand scheme, where the Vodafone brand is added at the end of the local brand. (i.e., TDC Mobil-Vodafone etc.)<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, Vodafone entered into a title sponsorship deal with the <a href="/wiki/McLaren" title="McLaren">McLaren</a> Formula One team, which traded as "Vodafone McLaren Mercedes" until the sponsorship ended at the end of the 2013 season.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 December 2011, it acquired the <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Berkshire" title="Reading, Berkshire">Reading</a> based Bluefish Communications Ltd, an <a href="/wiki/Information_and_communications_technology" title="Information and communications technology">ICT</a> consultancy company.<sup id="cite_ref-VGE-H-12_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VGE-H-12-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The acquired operations formed the nucleus of a new Unified Communications and Collaboration practice within its subsidiary Vodafone Global Enterprise,<sup id="cite_ref-VGE-H-12_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VGE-H-12-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> which will focus on implementing strategies and solutions in <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a>, and strengthen its <a href="/wiki/Professional_services" title="Professional services">professional services</a> offering.<sup id="cite_ref-VGE-H-12_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VGE-H-12-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2012, Vodafone announced an agreement to acquire <a href="/wiki/Cable_%26_Wireless_Worldwide" title="Cable &amp; Wireless Worldwide">Cable &amp; Wireless Worldwide</a> (CWW) for \xc2\xa31.04 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-VGE-H-09_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VGE-H-09-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Vodafone was advised by <a href="/wiki/UBS" title="UBS">UBS AG</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Barclays" title="Barclays">Barclays</a> and <a href="/wiki/N_M_Rothschild_%26_Sons" title="N M Rothschild &amp; Sons">Rothschild</a> advised Cable &amp; Wireless.<sup id="cite_ref-VGE-H-09_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VGE-H-09-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The acquisition will give Vodafone access to CWW\'s <a href="/wiki/Fiber-optic_communication" title="Fiber-optic communication">fibre network</a> for businesses, enabling it to take <a href="/wiki/Unified_communications" title="Unified communications">unified communications</a> solutions to large enterprises in the UK and globally; and expand its enterprise service offerings in emerging markets. On 18 June 2012, Cable &amp; Wireless\' shareholders voted in favour of the Vodafone offer, exceeding the 75% of shares necessary for the deal to go ahead.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 2 September 2013, Vodafone announced it would be selling its 45% stake in <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Wireless" title="Verizon Wireless">Verizon Wireless</a> to <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Communications" title="Verizon Communications">Verizon Communications</a> for $US130 billion, in one of the biggest deals in corporate history.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> With the proceeds from the deal, it announced a \xc2\xa319 billion Project Spring initiative to improve network quality in Europe and emerging markets like India.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2017, the company took measures to prevent its advertising from appearing within outlets focused on creating and sharing hate speech and fake news.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Adverts">Adverts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Adverts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Since 2010, the adverts feature two bees named Jack and Mike. Other adverts feature <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i> character <a href="/wiki/Yoda" title="Yoda">Yoda</a>. <a href="/wiki/Idris_Elba" title="Idris Elba">Idris Elba</a> does voice over for adverts. In 2015, the new slogan, \'Live Life on 4G\', was launched.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa_and_the_Middle_East">Africa and the Middle East</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Africa and the Middle East">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin-left:1em; text-align: center;">\n<caption>Networks in the Middle East and Africa\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background:#ececec;" colspan="2">Majority-owned\n</th>\n<th rowspan="5">\n</th>\n<th style="background:#ececec;">Minority-owned\n</th>\n<th rowspan="5">\n</th>\n<th style="background:#ececec;" colspan="2">Partner networks\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>DR Congo<sup>1</sup>\n</td>\n<td>Egypt\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Safaricom" title="Safaricom">Kenya</a>\n</td>\n<td>Bahrain\n</td>\n<td>Benin\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Ghana\n</td>\n<td>Lesotho<sup>1</sup>\n</td>\n<td>Sudan\n</td>\n<td>Iran\n</td>\n<td>Kuwait\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Mozambique<sup>1</sup>\n</td>\n<td>Qatar<sup>2</sup>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>Libya\n</td>\n<td>Tunisia\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vodacom_Tanzania" title="Vodacom Tanzania">Tanzania</a><sup>1</sup>\n</td>\n<td>South Africa<sup>1</sup>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>UAE\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="7" style="font-size:90%; line-height: 1em; background:#F2F2F2"><sup>1</sup>Majority stakes held through majority-owned Vodacom Group <br /><sup>2</sup>Effective ownership is not majority, but full control exercised by the group.\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">Egypt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Egypt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In November 1998, the Vodafone Egypt network went live under the name <a href="/wiki/ClickGSM" class="mw-redirect" title="ClickGSM">ClickGSM</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 8 November 2006, the company announced a deal with <a href="/wiki/Telecom_Egypt" title="Telecom Egypt">Telecom Egypt</a>, resulting in further co-operation in the Egyptian market and increasing its stake in <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Egypt" title="Vodafone Egypt">Vodafone Egypt</a>. After the deal, Vodafone Egypt was 55% owned by the group, while the remaining 45% was owned by Telecom Egypt.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kuwait">Kuwait</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Kuwait">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 18 September 2002, Vodafone signed a Partner Network Agreement with MTC group of Kuwait. The agreement involved the rebranding of MTC to <a href="/wiki/MTC-Vodafone" class="mw-redirect" title="MTC-Vodafone">MTC-Vodafone</a>. On 29 December 2003, Vodafone signed another Partner Network Agreement with Kuwait\'s MTC group. The second agreement involved co-operation in Bahrain and the branding of the network as MTC-Vodafone.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="South_Africa_.28Vodacom.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa_(Vodacom)">South Africa (Vodacom)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: South Africa (Vodacom)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 3 November 2004, the Company announced that its South African affiliate <a href="/wiki/Vodacom" title="Vodacom">Vodacom</a> had agreed to introduce Vodafone\'s international services, such as <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_live!" title="Vodafone live!">Vodafone live!</a> and partner agreements, to its local market.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2005, Vodafone announced that it was in exclusive talks to buy a 15% stake of VenFin in Vodacom Group, reaching agreement the following day. Vodafone and <a href="/wiki/Telkom_(South_Africa)" title="Telkom (South Africa)">Telkom</a> then had a 50% stake each in <a href="/wiki/Vodacom" title="Vodacom">Vodacom</a>. Vodafone now owns 57.5% of Vodacom after purchasing a 15% stake from Telkom.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 9 October 2008, the company offered to acquire an additional 15% stake in Vodacom Group from Telkom. The finalised details of the agreement were announced on 6 November 2008. The agreement called for Telkom to sell 15 per cent of its 50 per cent stake in Vodacom to the group, and demerge the other 35 per cent to its shareholder. Meanwhile, Vodafone has agreed to make Vodacom its exclusive sub-Saharan Africa investment vehicle, as well as continuing to maintain the visibility of the Vodacom brand. The transaction closed in May/June 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 May 2009, Vodacom entered the <a href="/wiki/JSE_Limited" title="JSE Limited">JSE Limited</a> stock exchange in South Africa after Vodafone increased its stake by 15% to 65% to take a majority holding, despite disputes by local trade unions.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2011, Vodacom rebranded with the Vodafone logo.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Qatar">Qatar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Qatar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In December 2007, a Vodafone Group-led consortium was awarded the second mobile phone licence in Qatar under the name "Vodafone Qatar". Vodafone Qatar is located at QSTP, the <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Science_%26_Technology_Park" title="Qatar Science &amp; Technology Park">Qatar Science &amp; Technology Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Commercial operations officially began on 1 March 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In February 2018 Vodafone Europe agreed to sell their stake in the Qatar joint venture.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ghana">Ghana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ghana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 3 July 2008, Vodafone agreed to acquire a 70% stake in <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Telecom" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghana Telecom">Ghana Telecom</a> for $900&#160;million. The acquisition was consummated on 17 August 2008. The same group-led consortium won the second fixed-line licence in Qatar on 15 September 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 15 April 2009, Ghana Telecom, along with its mobile subsidiary OneTouch, was rebranded as <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Ghana" title="Vodafone Ghana">Vodafone Ghana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="U.A.E.">U.A.E.</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: U.A.E.">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 28 January 2009, the group announced a partner network agreement with <a href="/wiki/Du_(telco)" class="mw-redirect" title="Du (telco)">Du</a>, the second-largest operator in the United Arab Emirates. The agreement involved co-operation on international clients, handset procurement, mobile broadband etc.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Libya">Libya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Libya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 24 February 2010, the group signed a partner network agreement with the second-largest operator in Libya, al Madar.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cameroon">Cameroon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Cameroon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 23 September 2016, Vodafone extended its activities to Cameroon by signing a partnership with Afrimax, a 4G-LTE telecommunications operator in Africa. Vodafone Cameroon Launched a "Youth Program" in the Universities to support and encourage the Cameroonian students.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Americas">The Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: The Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<dl><dt>Chile</dt></dl>\n<p>On 11 May 2008, Vodafone sealed a trade agreement with the Chilean <a href="/wiki/Entel_PCS" class="mw-redirect" title="Entel PCS">Entel PCS</a> Chile, in which Entel PCS has access to the equipment and international services of Vodafone, and Vodafone will be one of the trademarks of Entel for the wireless business. This step will give the Vodafone brand access to a market of over 15 million people, currently divided among two companies: <a href="/wiki/Telefonica" class="mw-redirect" title="Telefonica">Telefonica</a> <a href="/wiki/Movistar" title="Movistar">Movistar</a>, and Entel PCS.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Brazil</dt></dl>\n<p>In August 2013, Vodafone has started the MVNO operation in Brazil, as a corporative M2M operator.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dt>United States</dt></dl>\n<p>In the United States, Vodafone previously owned 45% of <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Wireless" title="Verizon Wireless">Verizon Wireless</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Joint_venture" title="Joint venture">joint venture</a> with <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Communications" title="Verizon Communications">Verizon Communications</a>, the country\'s largest mobile carrier. Vodafone branding was not used, however, as the CDMA network was not compatible with the GSM 900/1800&#160;MHz standard used by Vodafone\'s other networks and as Vodafone did not have management control over Verizon Wireless.  On 2 September 2013 Vodafone announced the sale of its stake to Verizon Communications for around $130 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2004 Vodafone made an unsuccessful bid for the entirety of <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Wireless_Services" title="AT&amp;T Wireless Services">AT&amp;T Wireless</a>, however, (Cingular Wireless) at the time a joint venture of SBC Communications and <a href="/wiki/BellSouth" title="BellSouth">BellSouth</a> (both now part of <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="AT&amp;T Inc.">AT&amp;T Inc.</a>), ultimately outbid Vodafone and took control of AT&amp;T Wireless (the combined wireless carrier is now <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Mobility" title="AT&amp;T Mobility">AT&amp;T Mobility</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2013, Vodafone was considered for acquisition by U.S.-based <a href="/wiki/AT%26T" title="AT&amp;T">AT&amp;T</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>  Ultimately, the deal did not move forward.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2014, Vodafone announced an agreement with <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile_US" title="T-Mobile US">T-Mobile US</a> to launch a <a href="/wiki/Mobile_virtual_network_operator" title="Mobile virtual network operator">mobile virtual network operator</a> (MVNO) service using its network, set to launch in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia-Pacific">Asia-Pacific</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Asia-Pacific">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin-left:1em; text-align: center;">\n<caption>Networks in Asia-Pacific\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background:#ececec;">Majority-owned\n</th>\n<th rowspan="10">\n</th>\n<th style="background:#ececec;" colspan="2">Partner networks\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Vodafone Limited">India</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>Japan\n</td>\n<td>Malaysia\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>Papua New Guinea\n</td>\n<td>Samoa\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>Singapore\n</td>\n<td>South Korea\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>Sri Lanka\n</td>\n<td>Taiwan\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>Thailand\n</td>\n<td>Turkmenistan\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>Uzbekistan\n</td>\n<td>Vietnam\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vodafone_Building_Near_Victoria_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The headquarters of Vodafone New Zealand in Auckland City</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In July 1993, <a href="/wiki/BellSouth" title="BellSouth">BellSouth</a> New Zealand\'s network went live. In November 1998, Vodafone purchased BellSouth New Zealand, which later became <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_New_Zealand" title="Vodafone New Zealand">Vodafone New Zealand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In August 2005, Vodafone launched 3G technology in New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-telecompaper2005_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telecompaper2005-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> On 9 October 2006, Vodafone New Zealand bought New Zealand\'s 3rd largest <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">internet service provider</a>, <a href="/wiki/IHug" class="mw-redirect" title="IHug">iHug</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In October 2013, Vodafone began its rollout of <a href="/wiki/4G" title="4G">4G</a> to provincial New Zealand, with the launch of the system in holiday hotspots around Coromandel.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In October 1993 <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Vodafone Australia">Vodafone Australia</a>\'s network went live. In December 2004, Vodafone Australia agreed to deploy high-speed <a href="/wiki/Multiprotocol_Label_Switching" title="Multiprotocol Label Switching">MPLS</a> backbone network built by <a href="/wiki/Lucent#Divisions" title="Lucent">Lucent Worldwide Services</a> using <a href="/wiki/Juniper_Networks" title="Juniper Networks">Juniper</a> hardware.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> In October 2005, it began launching 3G technology in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-telecompaper2005_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telecompaper2005-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> On 5 September 2008, Vodafone purchased Australia\'s largest bricks and mortar mobile phone retailer <a href="/wiki/Crazy_John%27s" title="Crazy John&#39;s">Crazy John\'s</a> adding 115 retail stores to its local operations.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 9 February 2009, Vodafone Australia announced a merger with 3/Hutchison via a joint venture company VHA Pty Ltd, which would offer products under the Vodafone brand.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> On 19 June 2009, Vodafone-Hutchison Australia (VHA) announced the end of its outsourcing of retail operations. VHA committed to buying back and managing its entire retail operation, including 208 Vodafone-branded retail outlets Australia-wide. This project was slated to be completed by 1 September 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 31 August 2009, VHA enabled an extended 900&#160;MHz 3G UMTS network which functions outside their 2,100&#160;MHz 3G network, boosting Vodafone\'s 3G population coverage from around 8% to around 94% on dual-band 900/2,100&#160;MHz 3G UMTS devices.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fiji">Fiji</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Fiji">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In July 1994 Vodafone Fiji\'s network went live. In July 2014, Vodafone sold its 49% shareholding of Vodafone Fiji to The Fiji National Provident fund. Under the terms of the deal, Vodafone Fiji retained its branding under a Partner Market Agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nadi_airport_-_Vodafone_office.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Nadi_airport_-_Vodafone_office.jpg/220px-Nadi_airport_-_Vodafone_office.jpg" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Nadi_airport_-_Vodafone_office.jpg/330px-Nadi_airport_-_Vodafone_office.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Nadi_airport_-_Vodafone_office.jpg/440px-Nadi_airport_-_Vodafone_office.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4920" data-file-height="2710" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nadi_airport_-_Vodafone_office.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vodafone shop at Nadi Airport, Fiji</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In 1999, J-Phone launched the J-sky mobile Internet service in response to <a href="/wiki/NTT_DoCoMo" title="NTT DoCoMo">DoCoMo</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/I-Mode" class="mw-redirect" title="I-Mode">i-Mode</a> service. It the became Japan\'s third-largest mobile operator and had introduced camera phones first in Japan. Vodafone then went on to acquire <sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> In December 2002 J-Phone\'s <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a> network went live. On 1 October 2003, J-Phone became \'Vodafone Japan\', and J-Phone\'s mobile internet service J-Sky became <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Live!" class="mw-redirect" title="Vodafone Live!">Vodafone Live!</a>. In March 2006, Vodafone sold Vodafone Japan to <a href="/wiki/SoftBank" class="mw-redirect" title="SoftBank">SoftBank</a>. In October 2006, SoftBank changed Vodafone Japan\'s name to \'<a href="/wiki/SoftBank_Mobile" class="mw-redirect" title="SoftBank Mobile">SoftBank Mobile</a>\'.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> On 17 March 2006, Vodafone announced an agreement to sell all its interest in Vodafone Japan to <a href="/wiki/SoftBank" class="mw-redirect" title="SoftBank">SoftBank</a> for \xc2\xa38.9&#160;billion, of which \xc2\xa36.8&#160;billion will be received in cash on closing of deal. Vodafone Japan later changed its name to <a href="/wiki/SoftBank_Mobile" class="mw-redirect" title="SoftBank Mobile">SoftBank Mobile</a>. In November 2010, Vodafone divested its remaining Softbank shares.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 28 October 2005, the Company announced the acquisition of a 10 per cent stake in India\'s <a href="/wiki/Bharti_Enterprises" title="Bharti Enterprises">Bharti Enterprises</a>, which operates the largest mobile phone network in India under the brand name <a href="/wiki/Bharti_Airtel" title="Bharti Airtel"><i>Airtel</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Then on 11 February 2007, the Company agreed to acquire a controlling interest of 67% in <a href="/wiki/Hutch_Essar" class="mw-redirect" title="Hutch Essar">Hutch Essar</a> for US$11.1&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, it agreed to sell back 5.6% of its <i>Airtel</i> stake back to the Mittals. Vodafone would retain a 4.4% stake in <i>Airtel</i>. On 21 September 2007, Hutch was rebranded to <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_India" title="Vodafone India">Vodafone</a> in India.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In May 2011, Vodafone Group Plc bought the remaining shares of <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_India" title="Vodafone India">Vodafone Essar</a> from Essar Group Ltd for $5&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In October 2013, it was reported by Reuters that Vodafone planned to invest as much as $2 billion (\xc2\xa31.2 billion) to buy out minority shareholders in Vodafone India.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By late January 2017, Vodafone Group\'s unit in India and <a href="/wiki/Idea_Cellular" class="mw-redirect" title="Idea Cellular">Idea Cellular</a> Ltd were in preliminary talks to merge.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> And on 20 March 2017, Vodafone announced that it was merging its Indian business with Idea, India\'s third-largest network, to create the country\'s largest operator with almost 400 million customers, accounting for 35% of the Indian cellphone service market.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Vodafone would own 45.1 percent of the new operator and Idea\'s parent company, the <a href="/wiki/Aditya_Birla_Group" title="Aditya Birla Group">Aditya Birla Group</a>, would own 26 percent. The deal valued Vodafone India at the equivalent of $12.6 billion and Idea Cellular at the equivalent of $11.02 billion. The deal would enable Vodafone to move its Indian subsidiary off its balance sheet, cutting the British group\xe2\x80\x99s net debt by the equivalent of almost $8.25 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Telecommunications_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Telecommunications (India)">Telecom ministry (DoT)</a> cleared the Vodofone\xe2\x80\x93Idea merger on 9 July 2018. On 31 August 2018 Vodafone Idea became a legal entity and the largest telecom service provider in India.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_Asia-Pacific">Other Asia-Pacific</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Other Asia-Pacific">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 3 November 2003, Singapore became a part of the community as <a href="/wiki/M1_Limited" title="M1 Limited">M1</a> was signed as partner network.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Then in April 2005, <a href="/wiki/SmarTone" title="SmarTone">SmarTone</a> changed the name of its brand to \'<a href="/wiki/SmarTone-Vodafone" class="mw-redirect" title="SmarTone-Vodafone">SmarTone-Vodafone</a>\', after both companies signed a Partner Network Agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> In January 2006, Indonesia, Malaysia, and Sri Lanka were added to the Vodafone footprint as Vodafone Group signed a partner network agreement with <a href="/wiki/Telekom_Malaysia" title="Telekom Malaysia">Telekom Malaysia</a>.  \nOn 6 February 2007, along with the partnership with <a href="/wiki/Digicel" title="Digicel">Digicel</a> Caribbean (see below), Samoa was added as a Partner Market. On 6 February 2007, Vodafone Group signed a three-year partnership agreement with <a href="/wiki/Digicel" title="Digicel">Digicel</a> Group. The agreement, which includes Digicel\'s sister operation in Samoa, will result to the offering of new roaming capabilities. The two groups will also become preferred roaming partners of each other.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 10 February 2008, Vodafone announced the launching of M-Paisa mobile <a href="/wiki/Money_transmitter" title="Money transmitter">money transfer service</a> on <a href="/wiki/Roshan_(Telecom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Roshan (Telecom)">Roshan\'s</a> (Afghanistan\'s largest GSM operator) network: Afghanistan was added to the Vodafone footprint.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Dtac" class="mw-redirect" title="Dtac">dtac</a> in Thailand is signed as a partner network of the Group on 25 March 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nar_Mobile" title="Nar Mobile">Nar Mobile</a> in Azerbaijan was signed as a partner network on 22 July 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Chunghwa_Telecom" title="Chunghwa Telecom">Chunghwa Telecom</a> of Taiwan was signed on 12 November 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2013, Vodafone together with <a href="/wiki/China_Mobile" title="China Mobile">China Mobile</a> participated in bidding for one of the two newly opened Myanmar Mobile licences.<sup id="cite_ref-ref2013040505_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref2013040505-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the beginning of September 2014, the Vietnamese mobile operator <a href="/wiki/Vinaphone" title="Vinaphone">Vinaphone</a> signed a strategic co-operation agreement with Vodafone.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin-left:1em; clear:right; text-align: center;">\n<caption>Networks in Europe\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background:#ececec;">Majority-owned\n</th>\n<th rowspan="16">\n</th>\n<th style="background:#ececec;" colspan="2">Partner networks\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Albania" title="Vodafone Albania">Albania</a>\n</td>\n<td>Austria\n</td>\n<td>Belgium\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Czech_Republic" title="Vodafone Czech Germany">Germany</a>\n</td>\n<td>Croatia\n</td>\n<td>Cyprus\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Greece" title="Vodafone Islands\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Ireland" title="Vodafone Ireland">Ireland</a>\n</td>\n<td>Iceland\n</td>\n<td>Latvia\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Italy"
