Malta">Malta</a>\n</td>\n<td>Macedonia\n</td>\n<td>Norway\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Netherlands" title="Vodafone Netherlands">Netherlands</a>\n</td>\n<td>Russia\n</td>\n<td>Serbia\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/KKTC_Telsim" title="KKTC Telsim">North Cyprus</a>\n</td>\n<td>Slovenia\n</td>\n<td>Sweden\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Portugal" title="Vodafone Portugal">Portugal</a>\n</td>\n<td>Switzerland\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Ukraine" title="Vodafone Ukraine">Ukraine</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Romania" title="Vodafone Romania">Romania</a>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Spain" title="Vodafone Spain">Spain</a>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Turkey" title="Vodafone Turkey">Turkey</a>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vodafone_UK" title="Vodafone UK">UK</a>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Vodafone Hungary was formed as a subsidiary company in July 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Mannesmann_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Mannesmann AG">Mannesmann AG</a>, completed on 12 April 2000, created subsidiaries in Germany and Italy, and increased the Group\xe2\x80\x99s indirect holding in <a href="/wiki/SFR" title="SFR">SFR</a>. The Vodafone brand in Italy was introduced as Omnitel-Vodafone in 2001, which became the primary brand in 2002; finally the current name <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Italy" title="Vodafone Italy">Vodafone Italia</a> was introduced in 2003, dropping "Omnitel" altogether.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2001, the Company acquired <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Ireland" title="Vodafone Ireland">Eircell</a>, the largest wireless communications company in Ireland, from <a href="/wiki/Eircom" class="mw-redirect" title="Eircom">eircom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Eircell was subsequently rebranded as <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Ireland" title="Vodafone Ireland">Vodafone Ireland</a>. In February 2002, <a href="/wiki/Radiolinja" title="Radiolinja">Radiolinja</a> of Finland joined as a partner network and later changed its name to <a href="/wiki/Elisa_Oyj" class="mw-redirect" title="Elisa Oyj">Elisa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, the company rebranded Japan\'s J-sky mobile internet service as <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_live!" title="Vodafone live!">Vodafone live!</a>, and in December 2002 the Vodafone brand was introduced in the Estonian market following the signing of a Partner Network Agreement with Radiolinja (Eesti), which later changed its name to Elisa.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2003, the company signed a group-wide partner agreement with <a href="/wiki/Mobilkom_Austria" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobilkom Austria">mobilkom Austria</a> and as a result Austria, Bulgaria, Croatia and Slovenia were added to the community.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> In April 2003, <a href="/wiki/Og_Vodafone" class="mw-redirect" title="Og Vodafone">Og Vodafone</a> was introduced in the Icelandic market.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> On 21 July 2003, Lithuania was added to the community, with the signing of a Partner Network Agreement with Bit\xc4\x97.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2004, Vodafone signed Partner Network Agreements with Luxembourg\'s <a href="/wiki/LUXGSM" class="mw-redirect" title="LUXGSM">LuxGSM</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> and with <a href="/wiki/Cyta" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyta">Cyta</a> of Cyprus. Cyta agreed to rename its mobile phone operations to Cytamobile-Vodafone.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> In April 2004, the Company purchased a British airtime provider, Singlepoint, for \xc2\xa3405m from John Caudwell\'s <a href="/wiki/Caudwell_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Caudwell Group">Caudwell Group</a>, adding approximately 1.5&#160;million customers and sites in Stoke-on-Trent to existing sites in Newbury (HQ), Birmingham, Warrington and Banbury.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In November 2004, Vodafone introduced <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a> services into Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2005, the Company bought the Czech mobile operator Oskar<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> which was rebranded as Oskar-Vodafone.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 October 2005, <a href="/wiki/Connex_GSM" class="mw-redirect" title="Connex GSM">Connex</a> in Romania was rebranded as Connex-Vodafone,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> and on 31 October 2005, the company reached an agreement to sell Vodafone Sweden to <a href="/wiki/Telenor" title="Telenor">Telenor</a> for approximately \xe2\x82\xac1&#160;billion. After the sale, Vodafone Sweden became a partner network.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> In December 2005, Vodafone won an auction to buy Turkey\'s second-largest mobile phone company, <a href="/wiki/Telsim" class="mw-redirect" title="Telsim">Telsim</a>, for US$4.5&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2006, the Company rebranded its Stoke-on-Trent site as Stoke Premier Centre, a centre of expertise for the company dealing with customer care for its higher-value customers, technical support, sales and credit control.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> On 22 February 2006, the Company announced that it was extending its footprint to Bulgaria with the signing of Partner Network Agreement with <a href="/wiki/Mobiltel" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobiltel">Mobiltel</a>, which is part of the <a href="/wiki/Mobilkom_Austria" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobilkom Austria">mobilkom Austria</a> group.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CentParkLepRoad.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/CentParkLepRoad.JPG/220px-CentParkLepRoad.JPG" width="220" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/CentParkLepRoad.JPG/330px-CentParkLepRoad.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/CentParkLepRoad.JPG/440px-CentParkLepRoad.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2912" data-file-height="2493" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CentParkLepRoad.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Ireland" title="Vodafone Ireland">Vodafone Ireland</a> in Dublin</div></div></div>\n<p>In April 2006, the Company announced that it had signed an extension to its Partner Network Agreement with BITE Group, enabling its Latvian subsidiary BITE Latvija to become the latest member of Vodafone\'s global partner community.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> On 30 May 2006, Vodafone announced the then-biggest loss in British corporate history (\xc2\xa314.9&#160;billion), and plans to cut 400 jobs; it reported one-off costs of \xc2\xa323.5&#160;billion due to the revaluation of its <a href="/wiki/Mannesmann" title="Mannesmann">Mannesmann</a> subsidiary.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> On 24 July 2006, the respected head of Vodafone Europe, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Morrow_(Executive)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bill Morrow (Executive)">Bill Morrow</a>, quit unexpectedly,<sup id="cite_ref-Bill_Morrow_Article_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bill_Morrow_Article-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> and on 25 August 2006, the Company announced the sale of its 25% stake in Belgium\'s <a href="/wiki/Proximus" title="Proximus">Proximus</a> for \xe2\x82\xac2&#160;billion. After the deal, Proximus remained part of the community as a Partner Network.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 5 October 2006, Vodafone announced the first single-brand partnership with <a href="/wiki/Og_Vodafone" class="mw-redirect" title="Og Vodafone">Og Vodafone</a> which would operate under the name <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Iceland" title="Vodafone Iceland">Vodafone Iceland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> and on 19 December 2006, the Company announced the sale of its 25% stake in Switzerland\'s <a href="/wiki/Swisscom" title="Swisscom">Swisscom</a> for CHF4.25&#160;billion (\xc2\xa31.8&#160;billion). After the deal, Swisscom would still be part of the community as a Partner Network.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> In December 2006, the Company completed the acquisition of Aspective, an enterprise applications systems integrator in the UK, signalling Vodafone\'s intent to grow a significant presence and revenues in the <a href="/wiki/Information_and_communication_technologies" class="mw-redirect" title="Information and communication technologies">information and communication technologies</a> (ICT) marketplace.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Munich_Leo_Parade_Vodafone.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Munich_Leo_Parade_Vodafone.jpg/220px-Munich_Leo_Parade_Vodafone.jpg" width="220" height="327" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Munich_Leo_Parade_Vodafone.jpg/330px-Munich_Leo_Parade_Vodafone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Munich_Leo_Parade_Vodafone.jpg/440px-Munich_Leo_Parade_Vodafone.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1076" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Munich_Leo_Parade_Vodafone.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Vodafone Lion on the L\xc3\xb6wenparade in Munich, Germany</div></div></div>\n<p>Early in January 2007, Telsim in Turkey adopted Vodafone dual branding as <a href="/wiki/Telsim_Vodafone" class="mw-redirect" title="Telsim Vodafone">Telsim Vodafone</a>, and on 1 April 2007, became <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Turkey" title="Vodafone Turkey">Vodafone Turkey</a>. In addition, Vodafone Turkey also gives service in Northern Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> On 1 May 2007, Vodafone added Jersey and Guernsey to the community, as Airtel was signed as Partner Network in both <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">crown dependencies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> In June 2007, the <i>Vodafone live!</i> mobile internet portal in the UK was relaunched. Portal pages which could previously be browsed at no cost were now charged for, and "bundled" data allowance was removed from existing contract terms.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> All users were given access to the full web rather than a \'<a href="/wiki/Walled_garden_(technology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Walled garden (technology)">walled garden</a>\', and Vodafone became the first mobile network to focus a media campaign on its newly launched mobile internet portal in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> On 1 August 2007, <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Portugal" title="Vodafone Portugal">Vodafone Portugal</a> launched Vodafone Messenger, a service with <a href="/wiki/Windows_Live_Messenger" title="Windows Live Messenger">Windows Live Messenger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Messenger" title="Yahoo! Messenger">Yahoo! Messenger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> At the end of 2007, Vodafone Germany was ranked 6th in Europe by subscriber numbers, whilst its Italian operation was listed as 10th. Vodafone UK was ranked 13th, whilst Spain was listed in 16th place.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 17 April 2008, Vodafone extended its footprint to Serbia as <a href="/wiki/Vip_mobile" title="Vip mobile">Vip mobile</a> was added to the community as a Partner Network,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> and on 20 May 2008, the Company added <a href="/wiki/VIP_Operator" title="VIP Operator">VIP Operator</a> as a Partner Network, thereby extending the global footprint to the Republic of Macedonia.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 30 October 2008, the company announced a strategic, non-equity partnership with <a href="/wiki/Mobile_TeleSystems" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile TeleSystems">Mobile TeleSystems</a> (MTS) group of Russia. The agreement adds Russia, Armenia, Turkmenistan, Ukraine, and Uzbekistan to the group\'s footprint.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 March 2009, it was announced that the group\'s Luxembourg partner has been changed: the agreement with LuxGSM was not renewed in favour of <a href="/wiki/Tango_(telecom)" title="Tango (telecom)">Tango</a>, the Luxembourg unit of another partner network, <a href="/wiki/Belgacom" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgacom">Belgacom</a> of Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 4 April 2011, Vodafone sold its 44% stake in <a href="/wiki/SFR" title="SFR">SFR</a>, the second largest operator in France, to <a href="/wiki/Vivendi" title="Vivendi">Vivendi</a> for \xe2\x82\xac7.95 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2013, the Spanish operations of Vodafone signed an agreement with <a href="/wiki/Orange_S.A." title="Orange S.A.">Orange S.A.</a> to co-invest \xe2\x82\xac1 billion in the expansion of Spain\'s <a href="/wiki/Fibre-optic_cable" class="mw-redirect" title="Fibre-optic cable">fibre-optic cable</a> broadband network, which would enable Vodafone to reach an additional 6 million customers in Spain by 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> On 24 June 2013, Vodafone announced it would be buying German cable company <a href="/wiki/Kabel_Deutschland" class="mw-redirect" title="Kabel Deutschland">Kabel Deutschland</a>. The takeover was valued at \xe2\x82\xac7.7 billion, and was recommended over the bid of rival <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Global" title="Liberty Global">Liberty Global</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In February 2014, Vodafone made an offer to acquire <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>\'s largest cable operator, <a href="/wiki/ONO_(Spain)" title="ONO (Spain)">ONO</a>, for total consideration, including associated net debt acquired, of \xe2\x82\xac7.2 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2015 <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Mobile_TeleSystems" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile TeleSystems">Mobile TeleSystems</a> and Vodafone expanded their 2008 strategic partnership; this resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Rebranding" title="Rebranding">rebranding</a> of MTS Ukraine to <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Ukraine" title="Vodafone Ukraine">Vodafone Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 31 December 2016, Vodafone Group\'s Dutch operations merged with <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Global" title="Liberty Global">Liberty Global</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Ziggo" title="Ziggo">Ziggo</a> brand, creating VodafoneZiggo Group Holding B.V.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2017, Vodafone was rated the worst mobile provider in the UK for the seventh year in succession in a "Which?" survey.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vodafone_Global_Enterprise"><span id="anchor_name"> Vodafone Global Enterprise</span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Vodafone Global Enterprise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Global_Enterprise" title="Vodafone Global Enterprise">Vodafone Global Enterprise</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vodafone-global-footprint.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Vodafone-global-footprint.jpg/220px-Vodafone-global-footprint.jpg" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Vodafone-global-footprint.jpg/330px-Vodafone-global-footprint.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Vodafone-global-footprint.jpg/440px-Vodafone-global-footprint.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2516" data-file-height="1372" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vodafone-global-footprint.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map showing the countries where Vodafone Global Enterprise has operations (coloured in red)</div></div></div>\n<p>Vodafone Global Enterprise is the business services division, and a wholly owned <a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">subsidiary</a> of Vodafone Group. It was established in April 2007 to provide <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_service" title="Telecommunications service">telecommunications</a> and <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a> services to large corporations.<sup id="cite_ref-VGE-H-10_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VGE-H-10-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VGE-H-02_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VGE-H-02-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VGE-H-04_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VGE-H-04-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The division offers integrated communication solutions in <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unified_communications" title="Unified communications">unified communications</a> and <a href="/wiki/Collaboration" title="Collaboration">collaboration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-VGE-H-10_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VGE-H-10-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VGE-H-02_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VGE-H-02-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Its services include domestic and international voice and data, machine-to-machine services, mobile email, mobile broadband, managed services, mobile payment and mobile recording.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2011, it acquired the <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Berkshire" title="Reading, Berkshire">Reading</a>-based Bluefish Communications Ltd, an <a href="/wiki/Information_and_Communication_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Information and Communication Technology">ICT</a> consultancy company.<sup id="cite_ref-VGE-H-11_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VGE-H-11-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The acquired operations formed the nucleus of a new Unified Communications and Collaboration practice within VGE,<sup id="cite_ref-VGE-H-12_37-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VGE-H-12-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> working on cloud computing and  <a href="/wiki/Professional_services" title="Professional services">professional services</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-VGE-H-13_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VGE-H-13-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Vodafone Global Enterprise operates in over 65 countries, with "Northern Europe" (based in London, United Kingdom), "Central Europe", "Southern Europe and Africa", "Asia Pacific &amp; Sub-Saharan Africa" (based in Singapore) and "Americas" geographical divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-VGE-H-01_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VGE-H-01-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> VGE\'s major customers include <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Post" title="Deutsche Post">Deutsche Post</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Linde_Group" title="The Linde Group">The Linde Group</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Unilever" title="Unilever">Unilever</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products_and_services">Products and services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Products and services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vodafone_shop,_Lands_Lane,_Leeds_(17th_December_2012).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Vodafone_shop%2C_Lands_Lane%2C_Leeds_%2817th_December_2012%29.JPG/220px-Vodafone_shop%2C_Lands_Lane%2C_Leeds_%2817th_December_2012%29.JPG" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Vodafone_shop%2C_Lands_Lane%2C_Leeds_%2817th_December_2012%29.JPG/330px-Vodafone_shop%2C_Lands_Lane%2C_Leeds_%2817th_December_2012%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Vodafone_shop%2C_Lands_Lane%2C_Leeds_%2817th_December_2012%29.JPG/440px-Vodafone_shop%2C_Lands_Lane%2C_Leeds_%2817th_December_2012%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1253" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vodafone_shop,_Lands_Lane,_Leeds_(17th_December_2012).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Vodafone shop selling a range of products in <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, England</div></div></div>\n<p>In October 2009, it launched Vodafone 360, a new internet service for the mobile, PC and Mac. This was discontinued in December 2011 after disappointing hardware sales.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> This was after the Director of Internet Services resigned in September 2010 tweeting "5 days before I leave Vodafone. Freedom beckons."<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> In February 2010, Vodafone launched the world\'s cheapest mobile phone known as Vodafone 150, intended to sell for below $15 (\xc2\xa310) in the developing world. It was initially launched in India, Turkey and eight African countries including Lesotho, Kenya and Ghana.<sup id="cite_ref-2005annual_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2005annual-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_money_transfer_services">Mobile money transfer services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Mobile money transfer services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In March 2007, <a href="/wiki/Safaricom" title="Safaricom">Safaricom</a>, which is part owned by Vodafone and the leading mobile communication provider in Kenya, launched a mobile payment solution developed by Vodafone.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By February 2008, the <a href="/wiki/M-PESA" class="mw-redirect" title="M-PESA">M-PESA</a> money transfer system in Kenya had gained 1.6&#160;million customers.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> By 2011 there were fourteen million M-Pesa accounts by which held 40 percent of the country\'s savings.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Following M-PESA\'s success in Kenya, Vodafone announced that it was to extend the service to Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The service here was launched on the Roshan network under the brand M-Paisa with a different focus to the Kenyan service. M-Paisa was targeted as a vehicle for <a href="/wiki/Microfinance" title="Microfinance">microfinance</a> institutions\' (MFI) loan disbursements and repayments, alongside business-to-business applications such as salary disbursement. The Afghanistan launch was followed in April 2008 by the announcement of further a further launch of M-PESA in Tanzania, South Africa<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> and India.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2012, Vodafone announced a worldwide partnership with Visa.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="mHealth_services">mHealth services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: mHealth services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In November 2009, Vodafone announced the creation of a new business unit focused on the emerging <a href="/wiki/MHealth" title="MHealth">mHealth</a> market (the application of mobile communications and network technologies to healthcare).<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> One of its early success stories is with the <a href="/wiki/Novartis" title="Novartis">Novartis</a>-led "SMS for Life" project in Tanzania, for which Vodafone developed and deployed a text-message based system that enables all of the country\'s 4,600 public health facilities to report their levels of <a href="/wiki/Anti-malarial" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-malarial">anti-malarial medications</a> so that stock level data can be viewed centrally in real-time, enabling timely re-supply of stock. During the SMS for Life pilot, which covered 129 health facilities over six months, stock-outs dropped from 26% to 0.8%, saving thousands of lives.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vodafone_Foundation">Vodafone Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Vodafone Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Vodafone Foundation is a recognised charity which supports and initiates projects which use mobile technology to benefit the vulnerable, using the slogan "Connecting for Good".<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> They often work in collaboration with other charitable groups. Below are some examples of their initiatives:\n</p>\n<ul><li>TECSOS \xe2\x80\x93 mobile phones have been adapted to allow victims of domestic violence to activate immediate contact with the emergency services if they are in danger</li>\n<li>Paediatric Epilepsy Remote Monitoring System \xe2\x80\x93 a monitoring system that allows physicians to remotely make patient observations</li>\n<li>Safe Taxi System \xe2\x80\x93 an initiative in Portugal that consists of technology that taxi drivers can use to alert police if they are in danger of being assaulted</li>\n<li>Learning with Vodafone Solution \xe2\x80\x93 technology that allows teachers in India to use graphical and multi-media content to enhance their teaching</li>\n<li>The World of Difference programme \xe2\x80\x93 successful applicants choose charities for which they work either full-time for two months or part-time for four months (minimum 15 hours a week). The charities are provided with \xc2\xa32,500, with each winner receiving the balance as a salary after NI and tax have been paid.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Newbury,_New_Vodafone_Headquarters_-_geograph.org.uk_-_5590.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Newbury%2C_New_Vodafone_Headquarters_-_geograph.org.uk_-_5590.jpg/220px-Newbury%2C_New_Vodafone_Headquarters_-_geograph.org.uk_-_5590.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Newbury%2C_New_Vodafone_Headquarters_-_geograph.org.uk_-_5590.jpg/330px-Newbury%2C_New_Vodafone_Headquarters_-_geograph.org.uk_-_5590.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Newbury%2C_New_Vodafone_Headquarters_-_geograph.org.uk_-_5590.jpg/440px-Newbury%2C_New_Vodafone_Headquarters_-_geograph.org.uk_-_5590.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Newbury,_New_Vodafone_Headquarters_-_geograph.org.uk_-_5590.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Part of the Vodafone campus in <a href="/wiki/Newbury,_Berkshire" title="Newbury, Berkshire">Newbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berkshire" title="Berkshire">Berkshire</a>; Vodafone\'s registered address and UK headquarters, and its world headquarters until 2009</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Senior_management">Senior management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Senior management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Gerry_Whent" title="Gerry Whent">Sir Gerald Whent</a>, at that time an Executive with Racal Electronics plc, was responsible for the bid for a UK Cellular Network licence. The Mobile Telecoms division was de-merged, and was floated on the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a> in October 1988 and Sir Gerald became Chief Executive of Racal Telecom plc. Over the next few years the company grew to become the UK\'s Market Leader, changing its name to Vodafone Group plc in the process.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Chris_Gent" title="Chris Gent">Sir Christopher Gent</a> took over as Chief Executive in January 1997, after Sir Gerald\'s retirement. Gent was responsible for transforming Vodafone from a small UK operator into the global operator, through the merger with the American AirTouch and the takeover of Germany\'s Mannesmann.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Arun_Sarin" title="Arun Sarin">Arun Sarin</a> was the driving force behind the Company\'s move into emerging markets such as Asia and Africa, through the purchases such as that of Turkish operator Telsim, and a majority stake in Hutchison Essar in India.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The fourth CEO, <a href="/wiki/Vittorio_Colao" title="Vittorio Colao">Vittorio Colao</a>, stepped up from Deputy Chief Executive in July 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Chief Executive</th>\n<th>Tenure\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Gerry_Whent" title="Gerry Whent">Sir Gerald Whent</a></td>\n<td>October 1988 \xe2\x80\x93 December 1996\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Chris_Gent" title="Chris Gent">Sir Christopher Gent</a></td>\n<td>January 1997 \xe2\x80\x93 July 2003\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Arun_Sarin" title="Arun Sarin">Arun Sarin</a></td>\n<td>July 2003 \xe2\x80\x93 July 2008\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vittorio_Colao" title="Vittorio Colao">Vittorio Colao</a></td>\n<td>July 2008 - September 2018\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Nick_Read" title="Nick Read">Nick Read</a></td>\n<td>Since October 2018\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_results">Financial results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Financial results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Vodafone reports its results in accordance with <a href="/wiki/International_Financial_Reporting_Standards" title="International Financial Reporting Standards">International Financial Reporting Standards</a> (IFRS). Financial performance has been as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-prelims_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prelims-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Year ended 31 March</th>\n<th>Turnover \xe2\x82\xacm</th>\n<th>Profit before tax \xe2\x82\xacm</th>\n<th>Profit for the year \xe2\x82\xacm</th>\n<th>Basic <a href="/wiki/Earnings_per_share" title="Earnings per share">eps</a> (pence)</th>\n<th>Proportionate customers (m)\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2017</td>\n<td>47,631</td>\n<td>2,792</td>\n<td>(6,079)</td>\n<td>(7.83)</td>\n<td>533.6\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2016</td>\n<td>49,810</td>\n<td>(190)</td>\n<td>(5,122)</td>\n<td>(20.27)</td>\n<td>462.0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2015</td>\n<td>48,385</td>\n<td>1,734</td>\n<td>7,477</td>\n<td>28.72</td>\n<td>446.0\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticisms">Criticisms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Criticisms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UK_Uncut_protest_outside_Vodafone,_Church_Street,_Liverpool.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="Protestors outside Vodafone shop." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/UK_Uncut_protest_outside_Vodafone%2C_Church_Street%2C_Liverpool.jpeg/220px-UK_Uncut_protest_outside_Vodafone%2C_Church_Street%2C_Liverpool.jpeg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/UK_Uncut_protest_outside_Vodafone%2C_Church_Street%2C_Liverpool.jpeg/330px-UK_Uncut_protest_outside_Vodafone%2C_Church_Street%2C_Liverpool.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/UK_Uncut_protest_outside_Vodafone%2C_Church_Street%2C_Liverpool.jpeg/440px-UK_Uncut_protest_outside_Vodafone%2C_Church_Street%2C_Liverpool.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UK_Uncut_protest_outside_Vodafone,_Church_Street,_Liverpool.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/UK_Uncut" title="UK Uncut">UK Uncut</a> protestors outside a Vodafone shop in <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tax_avoidance">Tax avoidance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Tax avoidance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In September 2010, an investigation by <i><a href="/wiki/Private_Eye" title="Private Eye">Private Eye</a></i> magazine revealed certain details of Vodafone\'s tax avoidance activities. It was reported that Vodafone routed the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Mannesmann" title="Mannesmann">Mannesmann</a> through a Luxembourg subsidiary, set up to avoid paying tax on the deal, and continued to place its profits in Luxembourg. Following a long legal struggle with <a href="/wiki/HMRC" class="mw-redirect" title="HMRC">HMRC</a> (during which a senior HMRC official, John Connors, switched sides to become head of tax at Vodafone), it was eventually agreed that Vodafone would pay \xc2\xa31.25&#160;billion related to the acquisition. Based on Vodafone\'s accounts, experts have estimated the potential tax bill written off as a result of the negotiations was over \xc2\xa36&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The news of this legal <a href="/wiki/Tax_avoidance" title="Tax avoidance">tax avoidance</a> sparked angry protests, beginning in October 2010 and ongoing as of April 2011, outside Vodafone shops across the UK, organised under the banner of <a href="/wiki/UK_Uncut" title="UK Uncut">UK Uncut</a>. The first protests caused the simultaneous closure of over a dozen stores, including the flagship Oxford Street branch.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2011, <i>Private Eye</i> magazine and The <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Investigative_Journalism" title="Bureau of Investigative Journalism">Bureau of Investigative Journalism</a> alleged that Vodafone\'s Swiss branches were run by a single part-time bookkeeper. The report claimed hardly any business was done from there, indicating that the main purpose of the Zug office was tax avoidance. The report claimed the money was borrowed from the Swiss branch of the Luxembourg company, allowing it to take advantage of Luxembourg\'s laws, which exempts foreign branches of companies from tax, and Swiss laws, which almost completely exempt local branches of foreign companies. According to the expose, this would have otherwise generated a British tax bill on a little over \xc2\xa32&#160;billion. It said Vodafone publishes a single, combined set of accounts for its Luxembourg subsidiaries and their Swiss branches. For the one company, profits worth \xc2\xa31.6&#160;billion were taxed at less than 1% in 2011, and the profits are likely to have been attributed to Switzerland. In its response to these allegations, Vodafone has said the Swiss branch has not been involved in Vodafone\'s global financing for a number of years. It is, therefore, irrelevant in respect to global financing arrangements.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Vodafone was also assessed a US$2.5&#160;billion tax over its acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Hutchison_Whampoa" title="Hutchison Whampoa">Hutchison Whampoa</a>\'s Indian assets in 2007, a demand that it contests. In January 2012, the highest Indian court ruled that Vodafone is not liable for taxes and penalties of up to \xc2\xa32.8&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> However, in February 2016 India\'s tax department sent Vodafone a renewed tax notice of \xc2\xa31.4bn. Following the siding of the Indian court with Vodafone in 2012, the government changed the law to allow firms to be retrospectively taxed.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications_blackout_during_the_Arab_Spring">Communications blackout during the Arab Spring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Communications blackout during the Arab Spring">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Vodafone was implicated in the violent suppression of pro-democracy protests in <a href="/wiki/2011_Egyptian_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Egyptian protests">Egypt\'s 2011 demonstrations</a>. On 27 January, Vodafone, responsible for much of Egypt\'s telecommunication infrastructure, shut off all voice and data services for Egyptian citizens and businesses at the request of the Egyptian Government under <a href="/wiki/Hosni_Mubarak" title="Hosni Mubarak">Hosni Mubarak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> On 28 January 2011, Vodafone complied with Egyptian government instructions to suspend Internet service "in selected areas" during a period of <a href="/wiki/2011_Egyptian_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Egyptian protests">anti-Mubarak protests</a>. The company issued a statement that "Under Egyptian legislation, the authorities have the right to issue such an order and we are obliged to comply with it."<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Vodafone also received public and media criticism for allowing the authorities to send mass pro-government messages via SMS over their network during the protests. One such message requested that "honest and loyal men" should "confront the traitors and criminals". Vodafone later issued a statement asserting that they had no choice but to allow the messages to be broadcast, and that they had complained to the Egyptian authorities about the practice.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> The Daily Telegraph of the UK reported, "The Egyptian government\'s action is unprecedented in the history of the internet."<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> US-based Internet intelligence firm Renesys stated, "in an action unprecedented in Internet history, the Egyptian government appears to have ordered service providers to shut down all international connections to the Internet."<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Vodafone Group CEO Vittorio Colao said the company was obliged by law to comply with the instructions of the Egyptian government.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> At the company\'s annual general meeting, on 26 June, the campaign groups Access and <a href="/wiki/FairPensions" class="mw-redirect" title="FairPensions">FairPensions</a> asked Vodafone to endorse a plan to prevent the company facing similar demands in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poor_customer_service">Poor customer service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Poor customer service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In Australia, particularly towards the end of 2010, Vodafone have been heavily criticised due to allegations of poor customer service and severe technical inadequacies, which earned them their nickname "Vodafail" \xe2\x80\x93 a website of the same name still exists.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> In response, they have developed a "new" network, and now provide a 30-day satisfaction guarantee.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unlimited_roaming_costs_on_stolen_phones">Unlimited roaming costs on stolen phones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Unlimited roaming costs on stolen phones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Vodafone UK, in common with other operators, has been criticised for holding customers on regular monthly billed contracts liable for almost unlimited <a href="/wiki/Roaming" title="Roaming">roaming</a> costs when their phones are stolen abroad, despite being seemingly able to limit costs of pay-as-you-go contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Breaches_of_consumer_protection_rules">Breaches of consumer protection rules</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Breaches of consumer protection rules">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In October 2016, Vodafone was fined a record \xc2\xa34.6m by <a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">Ofcom</a> for "serious" breaches of consumer protection rules.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> In April 2017, Vodafone continued to have major issues with customer service, with the CEO Nick Jeffery inviting customers with unresolved complaints to email him directly.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2017, <a href="/wiki/Citizens_Advice" title="Citizens Advice">Citizens Advice</a> undertook a mystery shopping exercise which found that Vodafone, along with <a href="/wiki/EE_Limited" title="EE Limited">EE</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hutchison_3G" class="mw-redirect" title="Hutchison 3G">Three</a>, were not reducing customers\' bills after fixed deals finished which meant that they were paying an extra \xc2\xa322 a month on average.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Surveillance_infrastructure">Surveillance infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Surveillance infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In June 2014, Vodafone revealed information about their and other telecommunication operators\' \'direct access systems\', content data and <a href="/wiki/Metadata" title="Metadata">metadata</a> interception programmes globally.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vodafone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41"
